  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_19bca3f8-6506-4320-9a61-91b2194887d8'
      });

  <span id="freeText17852907352206259926" style="display:none">We were in the square, in the square where I'd run, holding her, carrying her, telling her to stay alive, stay alive till we got safe, till we got to Haven so I could save her - But there weren't no safety, no safety at all, there was just him and his men...<br /><br />Fleeing before a relentless army, Todd has carried a desperately wounded Viola right into the hands of their worst enemy, Mayor Prentiss. Immediately separated from Viola and imprisoned, Todd is forced to learn the ways of the Mayor's new order. But what secrets are hiding just outside of town? And where is Viola? Is she even still alive? And who are the mysterious Answer? And then, one day, the bombs begin to explode...<br /><br />"The Ask and the Answer" is a tense, shocking and deeply moving novel of resistance under the most extreme pressure. This is the second title in the "Chaos Walking" trilogy.</span>

<a href="/questions/543070-my-major-beef-with-the-knife-of-never">My major beef with The Knife of Never Letting go was the writing style used on Todd. Ex: attenshyn (for attention) and musta (must have) It was a distraction for me. Does this happen in this book as well? Thanks.</a>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/473949-i-did-not-like-the-first-book-very-much-at">I did not like the first book very much at all. The reading style was interesting, the story line was different, I just felt like the pace was terrible and repetitive. Is it worth it to read the rest of the series?</a>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/50958333-grabahotchoc"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1451904304i/50958333._UY100_CR56,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/50958333-grabahotchoc">GrabAHotChoc</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I understand your concern in terms of the pace, but i truly do feel that if you plough on the pace becomes quicker and faster and in a way this book i<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I understand your concern in terms of the pace, but i truly do feel that if you plough on the pace becomes quicker and faster and in a way this book is extremely moving. You may not see it now, but reading on through the other books, the characters progress and grow and the voice of both Todd and Viola shine through. Hope this helped.<br />If you have any more questions, visit my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://chatiamirah.wix.com/grabahotchoc">http://chatiamirah.wix.com/grabahotchoc</a> <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_15').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_241849557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241849557" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241849557?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780763648374" href="/book/show/7849503-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241849557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12432717101703879116">okay, so i loved <i>the knife of never letting go</i> but this one was somehow even better.<br/><br/>oh, jeez, i am afraid i am just going to write a gushing fangirl review here. does anyone mind?<br/><br/>i will try to avoid saying anything too specific, because this book is such a gem, i want everyone to sort of discover its folds and depths for themselves.<br/><br/>because there is a great deal of depth up in here.<br/><br/>the action of this book takes place after a colossal thing happens which separates viola and todd. and this book is </span>
  <span id="freeText12432717101703879116" style="display:none">okay, so i loved <i>the knife of never letting go</i> but this one was somehow even better.<br><br>oh, jeez, i am afraid i am just going to write a gushing fangirl review here. does anyone mind?<br><br>i will try to avoid saying anything too specific, because this book is such a gem, i want everyone to sort of discover its folds and depths for themselves.<br><br>because there is a great deal of depth up in here.<br><br>the action of this book takes place after a colossal thing happens which separates viola and todd. and this book is a split-narrative between the two of them, as they are pursuing their individual paths to selfhood under extreme duress and uncertainty.<br><br>vague, right?<br><br>but it is so well-handled. ness can actually write! viola and todd sound like two different characters! and <i>fully developed</i> characters with insights and psychologies all their own, at that! and i love them both so much. fangirl squeee! <br><br>the scope of the book has widened. the first book starts out as a sort of smalltown pastoral with creepy-dark religious/cultish overtones, while this one expands to re-emphasize the earlier themes of colonialism and clannishness but to build upon those themes with the politics of war and love and betrayal and sacrifice (oh, the sacrifices...) and helplessness and growth and trust and - just all of it, all leading up to the most amazing cliffhanger of tolkien-esque proportions.<br><br>it made my head go "aaaahhhhhh!!!"<br><br>the best moments in these books are the small revelations, the tiny realizations. not even the big game-changing events, although those are phenomenal. but as viola and todd are separately coached under questionable authority figures, which are shaping their character, but still managing to retain their individual sparks that make them such strong characters, and while trying so hard just to get back to each other - the tiny reveals that pepper this story as they <i>bildungs</i> their <i>roman</i> are genuinely surprising and so devastating. shivery.<br><br>because they spend most of this novel apart, this becomes a novel about faith. faith in the beloved other. because while technically not a YA romance, because there isn't any kissing, it has the perfect shape to become one: the first book is spent fighting together towards a common goal, learning each others' strengths and weaknesses, making sacrifices (sob) to protect the Other, comforting each other and never letting the other lose hope or give up.it is a perfect foundation.<br><br>this chapter has them apart, developing their own personal codes in the middle of this new situation and creating a sort of armor around themselves to protect themselves from outside influence, to keep the faith in the other safe until they can be together again. which adds the layer of independence so fundamental to a successful romance. none of this <i>twilight</i> self-sacrifice twaddle.<br><br>it's just gorgeous. i hate the things that happen to todd throughout, as he struggles to balance his humanity while giving up portions of it just to stay alive. and although viola's situation seems less dangerous on the surface, it is only more adroitly manipulated, and so her ultimate realization/betrayal is even more powerful for it.<br><br><br>aaahhhhh!!!!<br><br><br>there is too much in this book and it is all in my heart.<br><br>i am trying to read the third book really slowly so i never have to leave this world.<br><br>there are probably more useful reviews out there. this is just be babbling. don't let me slow you down on your path to this book - go now!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12432717101703879116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4120652969306853183"><b>This trilogy is so freaking brutal I'm just sitting here trying to convince my heart to keep on.</b> I am so stressed. "Read books!" they said. "It'll be fun!" they said. Well I am. so. stressed. I really love that this had no sniff of sequel blues though, despite being...ya know, <i>blue</i> as a book itself. I do think it was a bit long and the tedium of Viola's and Todd's separate work situations could've been faster but other wise: WOW. I'M OBSESSED.<br/><br/><b>THINGS IN PARTICULARLY I LOVE:</b><br/>• never going to get ov</span>
  <span id="freeText4120652969306853183" style="display:none"><b>This trilogy is so freaking brutal I'm just sitting here trying to convince my heart to keep on.</b> I am so stressed. "Read books!" they said. "It'll be fun!" they said. Well I am. so. stressed. I really love that this had no sniff of sequel blues though, despite being...ya know, <i>blue</i> as a book itself. I do think it was a bit long and the tedium of Viola's and Todd's separate work situations could've been faster but other wise: WOW. I'M OBSESSED.<br /><br /><b>THINGS IN PARTICULARLY I LOVE:</b><br />• never going to get over the unique formatting and how great it is!<br />• Todd is a precious soft son and I love him so much<br />• also have decided Todd AND Viola are Hufflepuffs, fite me but I will not be changed<br />• I was surprised Viola' was narrating in this one?! but it was perfect and i loved her perspective<br />• plus her voice vs Todd's was really different which was great!<br />• Todd's raw emotion was just seeping onto every page and as much as I nearly hated him for things he did... I love him<br />• sobbing<br />• honestly the plot ---&gt; my feels didn't want to be together anyway<br />• i love how it contrasted two teams of war and how everyone sucks<br />• lowkey think the moral of this series is: men suck<br />• character development was A+ and I hurt<br /><br /><b>I loved the whole plot/trope of Viola and Todd being separated and so close yet so far.</b> It's enough to drive anyone uP THE WALL which is where I live now. Hello from up here. I am cross but also desperate to know what happens next. And there was so much emotion for both of them, because they're kind of each other's life rafts even when they're apart.<br /><br /><b>There is a lot of cloak-and-shadow-war going on in this one.</b> And I felt it was an interesting exploration of how tyrants often wheedle their people into believing they're doing the "right thing". This whole series is basically a dissection of power and control, over yourself and others, and it's SO interesting. Like not only do I love the characters and the plot, I adore the psychological aspect to!?<br /><br /><b>TODD AND VIOLA. LET ME CRY.</b><br />I pretty much adore Todd the most, but I think that's because we spent all of book 1 solely in his head. &lt;3 But this book is about breaking, and lies and twisting the knife into (my) heart. So I just ached for Todd. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Seeing him in shutdown mode after the spackle died, SO SO HURT. He's so depressed and so cut off and just ajfdkslad. And how he couldn't believe Viola came back to save him. Todddddd you're poor smol son. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I DID hate things he did though, and several times it was so freaking hard to forgive him for what he did. I know he was forced for most and super depressed/upset for a lot, but like...Todd??? No, Todd. (Also his relationship with his horse BROKE ME because it was like he was making up for all the time he was horrible to Manchee and I Just...*sobbing*)<br /><br />And <b>Viola</b> was so fantastic because she just never stopped. NEVER STOPPED. Even mortally wounded, she's like working to get out of here and fitting in and wanting to find Todd. Although Todd loves her about 100% and she loves him about 80% but I still adore them. And also Viola takes NO CRAP and I love that.<br /><br />(That little sniff of a triangle though?! I mean it wasn't a problem or a pain, but I was just: no.)<br /><br /><b>And would the mayor of Prentistown just pls go find a cliff and tumble off.</b> What a frikkin slimy snake of putrid muck. UGH I HATE HIM. I hate how he abuses someone and then gives back little privileges so he mind controls them into thinking he's helping. He really was a master of mind manipulation. It was really well written but MADE ME SO MAD. (I guess that's the point haha @ cait go cry somewhere else.)<br /><br /><b>MY HEART BROKE FOR THE SPACKLE</b>. But lowkey want 1017 and Todd to make up...<br /><br /><b>Also as much as I ship Todd/Viola, I don't see their relationship as being that romantic?!</b> I mean they are EVERYTHING together, and their love is legendary because it won't be shook, but it's like this epic ace relationship so far and that might be because they're young (like 15 right?) and everything is torture and WAR but also...heh. Let me headcanon their intense non-sexual love.<br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: this is torturous and dark and thrilling.</b> It's equal parts a war of the body and mind and I loved the contrast! I cried, I died inside, I shrieked a lot mentally and I was listening to an audiobook (which are A+ narrations btw) so basically I ended up doing origami long into the night because I COULDN'T STOP. I just wish it'd been a bit faster paced.<br /><br />ONTO BOOK 3 I CAN'T STOP</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8628213845202648745"><i> "So, who are you then, Todd Hewitt?" He says. "What makes you so special?" Now that, I think, is a very good asking." </i><br/><br/>What a crazy ending! <br/>I enjoyed this one a lot more than the first. I was more invested in Todd and Viola's characters, and accustomed to the writing style so I could fully focus on the story. Yay for second books!<br/><br/>So Todd and Viola found their way to <i> Haven </i> only to discover it was not the safe land they were hoping for. Pitted back against Todd's old nemesis Mayor Prentiss, Todd</span>
  <span id="freeText8628213845202648745" style="display:none"><i> "So, who are you then, Todd Hewitt?" He says. "What makes you so special?" Now that, I think, is a very good asking." </i><br /><br />What a crazy ending! <br />I enjoyed this one a lot more than the first. I was more invested in Todd and Viola's characters, and accustomed to the writing style so I could fully focus on the story. Yay for second books!<br /><br />So Todd and Viola found their way to <i> Haven </i> only to discover it was not the safe land they were hoping for. Pitted back against Todd's old nemesis Mayor Prentiss, Todd and Viola become separated - each on either side of an ongoing war. One between the people of Haven, calling themselves the Ask and those having escaped Haven and fighting against those in power - The Answer.<br /><br />This book was full of chilling scenes, including the torture of civilians, namely women. Some of the themes were extremely powerful, sexism, violence, terrorism, to name a few. <br />The Noise is still rife in this book - yet Mayor Prentiss has chosen to provide 'the cure' to some of his chosen favourites. I'm intrigued to see where Ness will go with the final book. This series seems to redefine genre - with elements of Sci-Fi, Fantasy, Dystopia and maybe even horror.<br /><br />The ending was mad! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I can't get over the arrival of a Spackle army - they are such weird creatures, I still don't fully understand them  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I've ordered the third book immediately - I need to know what happens!<br /><br /><i> "We are the choices we make" </i></span>

<div id="review_139355684" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139355684" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139355684?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406322477" href="/book/show/7003779-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dystopia-utopia">dystopia-utopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139355684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3484371432027019661">This stunning sequel to The Knife Of Never Letting Go manages to measure up to its predecessor in a way I never thought possible. After reading the first book, I felt sure that Ness would be incapable of delivering something equally brilliant. But he did.<br/><br/>This is an even more important book than part one, though admittedly not quite as fast-paced. It deals with feminism, terrorism, war and genocide. The alternating narrative works well and develops the reader's bond with the character of Viola. F</span>
  <span id="freeText3484371432027019661" style="display:none">This stunning sequel to The Knife Of Never Letting Go manages to measure up to its predecessor in a way I never thought possible. After reading the first book, I felt sure that Ness would be incapable of delivering something equally brilliant. But he did.<br /><br />This is an even more important book than part one, though admittedly not quite as fast-paced. It deals with feminism, terrorism, war and genocide. The alternating narrative works well and develops the reader's bond with the character of Viola. For me, it was an even darker novel than the first book, with Ness sparing no details on the violence and torture undergone by those suspected of being members of the Answer.<br /><br />It's a very shocking story and it questions what makes a person 'good' and whether an individual is solely responsible for their actions or if society and social factors can be blamed. Ness openly tackles the possibility of redemption in the most dire cases and he carefully blurs the lines between hero and villain. <br /><br />Is it okay to sacrifice one innocent person for the greater good? How about a thousand? Is terrorism a crime or a fight for freedom? The answers you think you have now may not be so easily applied when reading the book. It may make you question all that you've ever believed in.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3484371432027019661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1028818820?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310269" href="/book/show/6043849-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup">epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=romance-i-root-for">romance-i-root-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=this-cliffhanger-killed-me">this-cliffhanger-killed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028818820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15027520147284599839"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464529521i/19248322._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What would you choose if you had the faith of someone you love in your hands? <br/><br/><b>Would you betray your beliefs?</b><br/><br/>I must confess that the only <b>honest</b> answer I can give you is... <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418773676i/12891407._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Of course I'd be so <b>proud</b> if I was able to say that I'd do the right thing whatever it takes, and I want to think I'd do it. Really. Of course there are situations where what to do is obvious because one of the possibilities is utterly <i>bad</i>. But sometimes - <b>sometimes there's no such thing as a <i>right</i> choice</b>. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6043849.The_Ask_and_the_Answer__Chaos_Walking___2_' title='The Ask and the Answer (Chaos Walking, #2) by Patrick Ness' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Ask and the Answ</a></span>
  <span id="freeText15027520147284599839" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464529521i/19248322._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What would you choose if you had the faith of someone you love in your hands? <br><br><b>Would you betray your beliefs?</b><br><br>I must confess that the only <b>honest</b> answer I can give you is... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418773676i/12891407._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course I'd be so <b>proud</b> if I was able to say that I'd do the right thing whatever it takes, and I want to think I'd do it. Really. Of course there are situations where what to do is obvious because one of the possibilities is utterly <i>bad</i>. But sometimes - <b>sometimes there's no such thing as a <i>right</i> choice</b>. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6043849.The_Ask_and_the_Answer__Chaos_Walking___2_" title="The Ask and the Answer (Chaos Walking, #2) by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ask and the Answer</a> is <u>supposed</u> to be a children's book. Yes, for sure it is. I mean, that seems <i>crystal clear</i>, huh? The main characters <b>are</b> young, aren't they? <br><br>Yes... <b>But still</b>. Is it enough to tell? Really? <br><br>Because this book?! It actually made me think more than most of those I've read for <i>years</i>. And I read <b>a lot</b>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6043849.The_Ask_and_the_Answer__Chaos_Walking___2_" title="The Ask and the Answer (Chaos Walking, #2) by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ask and the Answer</a> gives rise to <b>ethical reflection</b> and disturbs us. <br><br><b>What is it that makes you a good person?</b> Is there a boundary line? Where is it, I'm asking, <b>where is it?</b> Is it what you <i>do</i>? What you <i>think</i>? What you <i>allow others</i> to do? <br><br><b>WHERE?</b><br><br>- Blur - <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"And they seem to unnerstand. That's the thing. They unnerstand way more than a sheep would."</b>
</blockquote><br>Make no mistakes, I hated Mayor Prentiss - <i>President</i> - Prentiss something fierce. I really did, from the beginning. Then, I never liked a lot this Mistress Coyle either. But these choices our characters must face? They're difficult. <b>Harsh.</b><br><br><b>*blush*</b> <i>Can I say it?</i> I only wanted for Todd and Viola to be safe. To be together. To be happy. Yes, I can be idealist that way.<br> <br>And maybe it makes me a coward, maybe it makes me weak, but -<br> <br>There was a moment I was just thinking one damn thing : <b>"Run!" <i>Fuck 'em all</i>, and run!</b> (shut up) But of course it'd be selfish. Of course life isn't so simple. And <i>of course</i> the story would be over, and way less interesting. I may be a romantic but not that dumb. I know that. <b>But still</b>. I'm just saying <i>I</i> thought about it. Fortunately for us, readers who want to be moved but <i>oh my god that's so harsh</i> - Fortunately for us, <b>Todd and Viola are amazing characters and oh so more stronger than me.</b><br><br><u>I'll let you know something</u> : This book is a gem, a real one, but <b>that was painful.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Cuz she's out there somewhere. (please be out there somewhere) (please be okay) (please)"</b>
</blockquote><br>I've said my heart ached for Todd in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2118745.The_Knife_of_Never_Letting_Go__Chaos_Walking___1_" title="The Knife of Never Letting Go (Chaos Walking, #1) by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">The Knife of Never Letting Go</a>? <u>Scratch that</u> : It just <b>
  <i>broke</i>
</b> in this one. <b>All over again</b>. I sure can't say that I agreed with all the choices he made. It'd be far from the true - some of his actions <i>are</i> really unforgivable <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[one word : 1017 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But, you know, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/370361.Patrick_Ness" title="Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">Patrick Ness</a> is such a genius - yes, because I know that the talent (or the lack of) of a writer plays a large part in our feelings towards the characters - that even if I hated Todd sometimes, I couldn't help but <b>love</b> him. Something fierce. <b>Whatever it takes</b>. <br><br><i>That's the whole point, huh?</i><br><br><i>
  <b>(Viola?)</b>
</i><br><br>You could think that this sentence, <i>"Love is stronger than anything"</i> is a pious platitude. You'd be right. I mean, we all know how this sentence is often used in romance novels to, you know, <i>try to hide the lack of plot</i>? <br><br>And yet you'd be so wrong. <b>This book is not a romance.</b> So then? Where does it lead us? <br><br><b>To a wonderful book about choices</b>. The choices we make and why we make them and <i>how can we be sure that we're right?</i><br><br><b>We just can't.</b><br><br>Let it be known that I will forever be destroyed by this quote. FOREVER -<br><blockquote>
  <b>"And someone calls, "Murderer!" from across the square. <br>But of course it can't be her - <br>But at least there's someone. At least there's someone."</b>
</blockquote> <br>... Because what are we hoping but for someone to speak up? I want to be that person, and even if I'm not gonna lie, it scares me to death, <b>I sure hope I would be, because what's the point of life if we can witness atrocities and just <i>stand</i> there?</b><br><br>I am in awe of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/370361.Patrick_Ness" title="Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">Patrick Ness</a>. His books are brilliant, and I'm already looking forward to reading the next. <i>Because of course there's a cliffhanger. </i> <u>Again.</u><br><br><b>
  <u>Edit 05/29</u>
</b> : I've started editing this review, but nothing could express my confusion and emotion more than the few words I wrote straight away. Perhaps it's for the best that my obsessional perfectionism can't influence everything. Perhaps sometimes, <b>beautiful sentences and neat organization would be nothing else but a lie.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460244805i/18718125._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10133650918537866122">Objectively, this whole series so far has been fabulously written. Really, really skilled author.<br/>Objectively, the book deserves five stars.<br/><br/>But... I'm only human, and subjectively I wanted to rip this book apart and then burn the shreds because it both makes me furious and scares me to death. Chaos Walking is the kind of story where every character is evil and corrupted in their own way and you're at a loss for someone to like/support. To make things worse, the main characters are children thrust</span>
  <span id="freeText10133650918537866122" style="display:none">Objectively, this whole series so far has been fabulously written. Really, really skilled author.<br />Objectively, the book deserves five stars.<br /><br />But... I'm only human, and subjectively I wanted to rip this book apart and then burn the shreds because it both makes me furious and scares me to death. Chaos Walking is the kind of story where every character is evil and corrupted in their own way and you're at a loss for someone to like/support. To make things worse, the main characters are children thrust into and twisted by a cruel world, driven to horrible acts by horrible circumstances. Through Ness' unique writing style, the reader can follow along right in Todd's head, and it all feels a little to close and real for comfort.<br /><br />This series really shook me, and I think I need a little time before I can finish the last installment.</span>

<div id="review_77077141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77077141" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77077141?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763644901" href="/book/show/6276045-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=tres-annoying">tres-annoying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77077141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10140745313461529729">I won't lie, I am really disappointed in and exhausted by this novel. "The Ask and the Answer" is very little like the first book in the trilogy "The Knife of Never Letting Go." <br/><br/>If the first one is a fast-paced chase kind of story, which keeps you hooked by gradual revelation of the New World's mysteries of Noise, Haven, Viola's origin, etc., this book is basically an account of a civil war between Mayor Prentiss's army and the resistance called here the Answer. The book raises various issues of</span>
  <span id="freeText10140745313461529729" style="display:none">I won't lie, I am really disappointed in and exhausted by this novel. "The Ask and the Answer" is very little like the first book in the trilogy "The Knife of Never Letting Go." <br /><br />If the first one is a fast-paced chase kind of story, which keeps you hooked by gradual revelation of the New World's mysteries of Noise, Haven, Viola's origin, etc., this book is basically an account of a civil war between Mayor Prentiss's army and the resistance called here the Answer. The book raises various issues of genocide, war ethics, torture, and holding onto one's identity under pressure. <br /><br />All issues are interesting, but I find myself surprisingly uninterested in them, mainly because in this book I am strangely detached from Todd and Viola. In these tough circumstances they are nothing more than naive petulant children used as pawns in various evil plans. They are described as so strongly attached that they are willing to do almost anything for one another and yet they are so easily led to mistrust each other.This mistrust constantly gets them and people around them in trouble, it's painful to read. I think pretty much in this book you simply can't find even one likable person. Todd is the one I dislike the most at this point. No matter how hard the author tries to make us believe that Todd still holds on to his innocence and thus is better than everybody else, it's pretty hard to swallow when you know what Todd has done for no good reason other than his dear girlfriend left him.<br /><br />In addition, there are the same plot holes as in the first book. I still don't understand the "specialness" of Todd, there is still a lot of build-up and allusions to various secrets that end up being not that interesting or important.<br /><br />I have to give Ness some credit for skillfully creating an atmosphere of urgency in his books and showing that nobody is truly innocent in war, but unfortunately, this just isn't enough for me. Gray shades are great in theory, but I would like to see some clearer morality in my books, especially in the books written for young adults. I find that at this point the only side I would want to succeed in the story is Spackle. Not sure if Ness meant it this way though...<br /><br />Reading challenge: #1 - N.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10140745313461529729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2569134511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12661029718760690615">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/10/25/the-ask-the-answer-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/><i> “In this world of numbness and information overload, the ability to feel, my boy, is a rare gift indeed.”</i><br/><br/>🌟 Yay, I was exactly the 60,000th thousand person to rate this!!<br/><br/>I guess you know the drill by this point, I usually compare the second book in a series with the first and see what improved and what didn’t.<br/><br/>🌟 I didn’t know what to expect after the ending of book 1 so my Ask was if I will enjoy this as much and the An</span>
  <span id="freeText12661029718760690615" style="display:none">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/10/25/the-ask-the-answer-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /><i> “In this world of numbness and information overload, the ability to feel, my boy, is a rare gift indeed.”</i><br /><br />🌟 Yay, I was exactly the 60,000th thousand person to rate this!!<br /><br />I guess you know the drill by this point, I usually compare the second book in a series with the first and see what improved and what didn’t.<br /><br />🌟 I didn’t know what to expect after the ending of book 1 so my Ask was if I will enjoy this as much and the Answer is apparently yes, it was a very good book.<br /><br />🌟 The writing is as good as book 1. These books are large (500-650 Pages) but the good news is that they feel like 300-400 pages instead. Patrick’s writing is easy to follow, full of suspense and can be poetic at the same time.<br /><br /> <i>“We are the choices we make. And have to make. We aren’t anything else.”</i><br /><br />🌟 The Pacing in book 1 was faster which is always a plus for me, the pace here is slower but not too slow so it is still enjoyable.<br /><br />🌟 There weren’t many new characters but the characters we know developed and I expected the change in some characters which was awesome and devil!<br /><br />🌟 Every one were talking about the plot twists in this book, I saw most of them before they happened and specially at the ending I was like what if this and that happened, that would be terrific and guess what? It did happen 😀<br />I liked how this was much darker than book 1 and some of the scenes were graphic so beware, I don’t think it is a suitable book for younger children. I discovered lately that I really love darker reads just because they are more realistic, the real world is not sunshine and flowers!<br /><br />🌟 The world also expanded and I think we are getting more of it in the next book.<br /><br />🌟 Summary: The Ask and the Answer was as almost as good as book 1, if you liked book 1 then the series is definitely worth continuing. It was slower paced, darker and more twisted. The story is balanced and I can’t wait to know how it ends.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15046380824895072485"><s>One taught me love, one taught me patience, one taught me pain.</s><br/><b>These books are only teaching me PAIN and STRESS</b></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_132138355" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132138355" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411956191p2/1219253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132138355?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763644901" href="/book/show/6276045-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=blog">blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132138355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15775192688409990239">**Some spoilers for those who have not read the first book**<br/><br/>I just wrote an exhausting review of this novel, but Goodreads screwed me and lost the entire thing. Pissed does not even begin to cover what I feel right now. All of that brilliance, now lost to the cyberspace void forever. <br/><br/>I didn't so much read the first book in this series, <i>The Knife of Never Letting Go</i>, as inhaled it. Original and disturbing, Ness is not afraid to take some risks as he tells the story of Todd Hewitt, a boy about to </span>
  <span id="freeText15775192688409990239" style="display:none">**Some spoilers for those who have not read the first book**<br /><br />I just wrote an exhausting review of this novel, but Goodreads screwed me and lost the entire thing. Pissed does not even begin to cover what I feel right now. All of that brilliance, now lost to the cyberspace void forever. <br /><br />I didn't so much read the first book in this series, <i>The Knife of Never Letting Go</i>, as inhaled it. Original and disturbing, Ness is not afraid to take some risks as he tells the story of Todd Hewitt, a boy about to become a man in Prentisstown--a town inhabited only by men. As we read, we find out that Todd lives on a colony planet so distant from Earth that it takes decades to get there. Upon arrival, the first colonists went to war with the indigenous inhabitants, the Spackle. In a desperate effort to defeat the invaders, the Spackle release a germ that kills all of the women. The men survive, but with a strange side-effect: they can hear each other's internal monologue. At least this is the story Todd was always told, but when he discovers a real girl in the swamp Todd is forced to flee for his life and learns that everything he thought was true is a lie.<br /><br /><i>The Ask and the Answer</i> picks up where <i>The Knife of Never Letting Go</i> left off. Todd and Viola, whose uneasy truce forged a devoted friendship, are separated when Mayor Prentiss (the antagonist from the first novel) names himself President, quarantines the women from the men, and establishes martial law in New Prentisstown. As Mayor Prentiss exerts his power, a female rebel force known as the Answer rises against him, and Viola finds herself swept up by their cause. Meanwhile, Todd is forced to do President Prentiss's bidding in order to keep Viola safe. He's put in charge of managing the enslaved Spackle workforce being used to build the New Prentisstown envisioned by the President.<br /><br />What is so fascinating about the novel is how Ness explores the brainwashing and mind games employed by each side as they use Viola and Todd as expendable pawns in their quest for victory. Viola struggles with the terroristic tactics used by the Answer against innocent civilians in the name of their cause, while Todd is forced to face his shame in killing a Spackle in the first novel as he witnesses the dehumanizing treatment of the thinking and feeling alien race. As Viola and Todd try to navigate the labyrinthine truths, loyalties, and beliefs that are relics from a war that occurred before either of them were born, they begin to question themselves and their trust in each other. This psychological complexity is heightened by the fact that the reader still isn’t sure who the bad guys and who the good guys are—if, in fact, there are any good guys. There are no easy answers and Ness forces readers to think through the complex issues of war, justifiable violence, and racism. <br /><br />Cross posted at <a href="http://viiamanda.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Insignificant Cinder</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15775192688409990239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17318539108421406844">Patrick Ness's writing is a thing of magic. He aptly portrayed the horrors of civil war on both sides, and how war has no clear "good guy" and "bad guy". The psychological aspect of this book is intense, being in the minds of both Viola and Todd as they try to pave a path for themselves in the hell that surronds them is both riveting and humbling. </span>

          </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310269" href="/book/show/6043849-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2098381-heather?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81299854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16753592728136806575">Ugh, I just can't do it. This book is contrived and ridiculous. The characters of Todd and Viola have reached a level of stupidity that I didn’t think was possible. I was put off by the first chapter, but continued to read for another 50 pages before I finally chucked it. Enough is enough. I had already ignored my instincts by picking this book up in the first place. Having read and been let down by book one, I was hoping that Ness would redeem himself. But alas, no such luck. Not only has Ness </span>
  <span id="freeText16753592728136806575" style="display:none">Ugh, I just can't do it. This book is contrived and ridiculous. The characters of Todd and Viola have reached a level of stupidity that I didn’t think was possible. I was put off by the first chapter, but continued to read for another 50 pages before I finally chucked it. Enough is enough. I had already ignored my instincts by picking this book up in the first place. Having read and been let down by book one, I was hoping that Ness would redeem himself. But alas, no such luck. Not only has Ness failed to create likable characters, he has massacred any redeeming quality in Todd or Viola in order to create a plot for his series. He should have left well enough alone, and ended this story in The Knife of Letting Go. I detest authors who rely on character idiocy to move their plot forward almost as much as I loath this book. If you aren't looking for any type of rhyme or reason, just itching for someone to get beat or killed, then by all means, read on, otherwise, read at your own peril.<br /><br /><br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer280941283" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9734345798462410684"><i>“So who are you then, Todd Hewitt? What makes you so special?”</i><br/>Where to start, where to start? In that first chapter, I was just <i>so proud</i> of you Todd. I feel like we’ve come a long way and it just never stops for you does it?<br/><br/>But seriously, where to start? I thought the last book was good. This one is <u>better</u>. Like, sell your aunt and your soul to the devil kind of good. It's just so full of <i>stuff</i>.<br/><br/>First off, despite my many attempts, I could never guess what would happen. When I gave up trying and </span>
  <span id="freeText9734345798462410684" style="display:none"><i>“So who are you then, Todd Hewitt? What makes you so special?”</i><br />Where to start, where to start? In that first chapter, I was just <i>so proud</i> of you Todd. I feel like we’ve come a long way and it just never stops for you does it?<br /><br />But seriously, where to start? I thought the last book was good. This one is <u>better</u>. Like, sell your aunt and your soul to the devil kind of good. It's just so full of <i>stuff</i>.<br /><br />First off, despite my many attempts, I could never guess what would happen. When I gave up trying and just went with it, it was still like running into a brick wall with your eyes closed. You knew it was somewhere but you didn't know where. In fact it was like running into <i>MULTIPLE</i> brick walls.<br /><br />The characters were even better than before. Not only do we get to hear from Viola's point of view (who is better than I could've hoped for) but all the characters are well developed and waaaay too realistic. I also developed some weird emotions for Davy Prentiss- seriously, right from the start. I just wanted to hug him though he was such an ass. But most of all, Todd. Sweet Todd. You scared me Todd. I got wrinkles from you Todd. <b>DON'T DO THAT TO ME AGAIN TODD!</b><br /><br />I'm sort of speechless. And still, after everything... I miss Manchee. Angharrad was sweet but if anything it made me miss Manchee even more. Poo? Todd? Poo? Manchee would've stopped this from happening. He was a <i>bloody good dog</i>. </span>

    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_2039546916" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2039546916" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2039546916?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310269" href="/book/show/6043849-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=post-apocalipse">post-apocalipse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2039546916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10220702405487467404"><b>*** 2.75 ***<br/><br/>A buddy with my friends at the MacHalos, because we obviously hate ourselves... </b><br/><br/>I am not going to write a real review for this one, because if it continues in the same vain, I will have to repeat myself when I finish the third and last book in the series. I am just frustrated...<br/><br/>Usually, when I read dystopian YA of substance, I am full of emotions which propel me to inspiration, and I have no problems putting them down in a review. Usually most of those feelings are positive. And just</span>
  <span id="freeText10220702405487467404" style="display:none"><b>*** 2.75 ***<br /><br />A buddy with my friends at the MacHalos, because we obviously hate ourselves... </b><br /><br />I am not going to write a real review for this one, because if it continues in the same vain, I will have to repeat myself when I finish the third and last book in the series. I am just frustrated...<br /><br />Usually, when I read dystopian YA of substance, I am full of emotions which propel me to inspiration, and I have no problems putting them down in a review. Usually most of those feelings are positive. And just as always, I try to balance my personal feelings with objective overview of the qualities of writing, plot, storytelling and so on... But sometimes, like right now, my emotions let me down and my objectivity starts failing...<br /><br />I feel like with the exception of couple of books, in the last couple of weeks I have fallen into a well of depression, dispair, and unlikable characters, and there is no one to throw me a line to drag myself out of it... I am becoming convinced that there is a wave of writers who have decided that having a great style and flawless control of their craft, they are going to use it to depress their readers. The do that by barraging them with slightly veiled truths of historical and contemporary human mistakes and failures, putting them in made up worlds, dressing them up as fables, and condensing them into powerful concentrates, serving them usually as trilogies, every one of them chipping away at our faith in humanity... All are good but also bad, all are apathetic, all are easily thrown out of balance, and everything goes as long as survival is guaranteed, to hell with higher values, dignity and beliefs! Those are the first victims of the battle for survival...<br /><br />Once again an obviously talented author is putting his talent to work at convincing us that personal feelings of love, selfish desire to be with the one you love no matter how many people would be sacrificed for it, come before the lives of others. As long as you get what you want, the world can burn... I wonder, is that what those authors see when they look into the world around them? Do their work give the readers a justification for their sense of entitlement? Or is it an attempt at a cautionary tale gone wrong? I am not sure anymore, and honestly, I am to tired of negativity with no true promise of redemption to care. ... <br /><br />I am so saddened that we had to witness the complete deconstruction and degradation of couple of promising characters... At the moment I feel contempt​ for the two "protagonists", hatred for most of the adults, and dejection with the human character. Weaknesses, gullibility, stupidity, willing complicity, enslavement, greed, strive for power... Kill less you get killed, never leave an enemy alive or they will come back to haunt you... Never mind that the label of "enemy" could be put on anyone who happens to disagree with you... I get it! We are all horrible people and we do bad things despite wanting to be good, although obviously we have no idea what being good means! I hear it loud and clear! You guys have pounded it over and over into our brains. Now, WHAT SHOULD ALL OF US DO ABOUT IT? What do YOU want us to come away with after reading your work. What is the point? It is not entertaining, so we can say we spend some fun times with the book, it is not "enjoyable", since there is not an ounce of joy in the whole series, at least not for now. Should we feel good for coming out of it disillusioned and depressed, angry and frustrated??? If that is the goal, congratulations! You have succeeded! Has it become impossible to write something dystopian but still convey a sense of honor and a spark of hope? I know that is not true and this is why I reach for the next book in the series. Because I have hope that there will be some light in the end of the tunnel and a gifted storyteller like Mr. P. Ness will not waste his and our time with books aimed at bringing us down. Reality does a good enough job at doing just that, and this is why we look for inspiration and emotional guidance in books.... <br /><br />I am disappointed with this book, but I am invested enough to want to read the finale. I hope it is as good as all those great reviews make it out to be! <br /><br />Now I wish you all to find a book that makes you feel HAPPY! We all need it🙂🙂🙂...</span>
  <a data-text-id="10220702405487467404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310269" href="/book/show/6043849-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">hunger games lovers; shusterman lovers; YA dystopian</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Isamlq by: </span>
      paolo ramirez (mwah-mwah,) tina, aaron vincent

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133389945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3805376593136894884">I imagine Viola, reluctant healer, the worst in fact, bumbling around; Todd working, slaving away. And I imagine their growing closeness despite everything that’s going on around them; despite the forced physical distance between them. <br/><br/>This book is a such a visceral experience. And it's more. I read it and I see everything in my mind’s eye. Not stills; I have a movie playing in my head. I sort of gag when I think of the stench from the Spackles’ corner in the morning. I can almost catch a whiff </span>
  <span id="freeText3805376593136894884" style="display:none">I imagine Viola, reluctant healer, the worst in fact, bumbling around; Todd working, slaving away. And I imagine their growing closeness despite everything that’s going on around them; despite the forced physical distance between them. <br /><br />This book is a such a visceral experience. And it's more. I read it and I see everything in my mind’s eye. Not stills; I have a movie playing in my head. I sort of gag when I think of the stench from the Spackles’ corner in the morning. I can almost catch a whiff of smoke after all those bombs go off. I can imagine how sticky the blood must be when Viola’s mends someone’s wounds. I tear up when I think of how they both feel: betrayed, abandoned, alone… And I try to wrap my mind around what the Noise must be like, or what the President’s scarier, controlled Noise must be like. <br /><br />But I am not imagining how upset I am at the turn of events. I really do choke up a bit at where the two end up. And I’m left feeling so many, many things: angry, sad, confused, a bit more sad, and whole lot more angry. No sophomore slump here. <b>None.</b> <br /><br />As Todd would say, it is effing amazing (and I didn't really say effing either.) <br /><br /><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_276412707" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/276412707" />
    <a title="Rachel Hartman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4545538-rachel-hartman"><img alt="Rachel Hartman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442465555p2/4545538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/276412707?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Hartman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Hartman" href="/user/show/4545538-rachel-hartman">Rachel Hartman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310269" href="/book/show/6043849-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer276412707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11558427193624238179">Most of the things I had issues with in the first book aren't a factor here, except for one. And it's kind of a big one. I'm going to have to meditate upon this for a time before I can write a proper review. Over all, though, I liked this one much better. Ness does relentlessly horrible like nobody else, and I say that with all the love and respect in the world.<br/><br/>*****************<br/><br/>AVAST, YE SCURVY DOGS, THAR WILL BE SPOILERS! Yaaarrr! I don't know why I hate the Global Spoiler Warning, I just do. I</span>
  <span id="freeText11558427193624238179" style="display:none">Most of the things I had issues with in the first book aren't a factor here, except for one. And it's kind of a big one. I'm going to have to meditate upon this for a time before I can write a proper review. Over all, though, I liked this one much better. Ness does relentlessly horrible like nobody else, and I say that with all the love and respect in the world.<br /><br />*****************<br /><br />AVAST, YE SCURVY DOGS, THAR WILL BE SPOILERS! Yaaarrr! I don't know why I hate the Global Spoiler Warning, I just do. If we had the option to dance a spoiler hornpipe instead, I would take it. I encourage you to imagine me leaping about piratically for a few moments. SPOILERS, SPOILERS, SPOILERS, yo HO!<br /><br />If that didn't scare you off, there's really nothing I can do for you.<br /><br />******************<br /><br />I loved this book. Loved it really hard. If you will recall my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148347999" rel="nofollow noopener">The Knife of Never Letting Go</a>, I loved that book a lot, too. I also hated it, and the result was the most passionate three stars I've ever given a book.<br /><br />Many of my problems with the first book do not occur here. No dogs are killed (BOOHOOHOO! MANCHEE!)(I will never get over that! Never!). The narrative is in first person present tense again, but there are two narrators. Viola's voice is a bit more articulate, which is kind of a relief, but more importantly, they're not keeping secrets from the reader. That was my very biggest beef before, that Todd was learning things in real time and magically having the ability to conceal that from the reader. That struck me as cheating.<br /><br />I was irritated with the crazy, indestructible Aaron before. One could argue that Mayor Prentiss is both of those things - his ability to wriggle out of tight places is a bit uncanny, and yes, he's not what most of us would consider entirely sane. Even so, I found him much more subtle and sophisticated than Aaron and understandable to a degree Aaron simply was not.<br /><br />Best of all, however, is the fact that the Mayor isn't the only evil. There are others, and every single one is ambiguous. Every single one of them raises interesting philosophical questions. Does fighting against an evil necessarily mean you're good? Are there necessary evils? Where is the line between freedom fighting and terrorism? Why show mercy to the oppressed if they're not grateful? To what extent is any individual expendable? To what extent is caring a weakness? How can you control people through manipulation of information, and how can an individual fight back against that?<br /><br />That's the part of the book I loved, this exploration of war and what it was doing to everyone. I don't think I've ever read a book that dug into both sides in quite this way, showing the psychic cost, how things escalate, how war takes on a life of its own that nobody can control. It was brilliant and horrifying.<br /><br />It was the end that knocked off a star, for me. Because there it was again, staring me right in the face, this notion of Todd as somehow "innocent" and "not a killer".<br /><br />HE KILLED A SPACKLE IN THE FIRST BOOK. I had a problem with it in THAT book, and here it is again. Todd can't kill! Um, gee, yes he DID.<br /><br />That, to me, sent the ending completely off the rails. I thought Viola forgave him too easily. I thought the psychology and explanation of him retaining his ability to feel things all through the horrors (when he turned his emotions OFF? I couldn't wrap my brain around that contradiction), the assertion that this somehow made him "innocent" where the others were monsters... that just didn't add up to me.<br /><br />Here's where I wish I had the book in front of me, and where I'm just going to have to come back later and explain things better. There were two quotes that really stood out as thesis statements, as if the whole book were some kind of geometric proof, a+b+c ergo CONCLUSION. And it didn't add up for me. The thesis statements were great -- one about love being a strength instead of a weakness, one about living in a world of information overload and how do you decide what's important. They were beautiful. They just weren't the answer to the equation I felt had been set up in the text.<br /><br />I think Todd and Viola would both have come out of this a lot more damaged than they seem to be. I get that they love each other; I get that he's trying to say something about how powerful love is (I suspect Davy Prentiss is able to do good in the end because he loves Todd, even though it's never spelled out exactly). Yes, love is powerful. But hurt is also powerful, and I can't quite accept that they're able to forgive each other and be quite that unshakeably bonded after all that they've been through.<br /><br />I'm still going to read the next one, though. And again: there was a lot to love in this. A lot of horrible, painful, well-done stuff to love. Whether you find the ending completely psychologically believable or not, there's a lot to think about in this book, and that's really what I'm in it for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11558427193624238179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1617593449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1617593449" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1617593449?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310269" href="/book/show/6043849-the-ask-and-the-answer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=dystopia-yes-pls">dystopia-yes-pls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1617593449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17479818025706631711">Stockholm Syndrome, anyone?<br/><br/>The Mayor has the upper hand and a stronger mind than anyone. I feel sorry for Tod and Viola for the most part, and the telepathy angle is growing a bit more interesting, but it's really the descent into evil that captures most of my imagination.<br/><br/>As it should, I'm sure. This dystopian SF was designed for the YA crowd and while it is very decent for what it is, the plot is not quite as strong as the characterizations and the world building is kinda lacking. <br/><br/>If you're loo</span>
  <span id="freeText17479818025706631711" style="display:none">Stockholm Syndrome, anyone?<br /><br />The Mayor has the upper hand and a stronger mind than anyone. I feel sorry for Tod and Viola for the most part, and the telepathy angle is growing a bit more interesting, but it's really the descent into evil that captures most of my imagination.<br /><br />As it should, I'm sure. This dystopian SF was designed for the YA crowd and while it is very decent for what it is, the plot is not quite as strong as the characterizations and the world building is kinda lacking. <br /><br />If you're looking for answers, look elsewhere. The Answer is just the rebels made up of mostly women. The question, at least in my mind, is what causes men to turn into cattle, whether it's the mayor turning otherwise intelligent people into subservients or what really happened to all the others that are literally being kept in pens.<br /><br />Lots of emotions flying about everywhere and I feel like I should be feeling a lot of pathos for the MC's, but unfortunately, I'm either in the wrong place to enjoy this or it just kinda feels a bit average. Perhaps I'm just getting tired of reading the same kinds of stories in certain markets. Maybe it's just a little too simple for my tastes. This is kind of a disappointment from the previous book in the series. *sigh*</span>
  <a data-text-id="17479818025706631711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
